A reader searching "Gateron Oil King", "GMK Olivia", or "Mode Sonnet" gets 0 results unless an article happens to mention the name — the part detail pages at `/part/[kind]/[slug]` are unreachable via the site's primary discovery surface.
  - **Phase 33 signal**: The "Find your switch" quiz routes home-page users directly to `/part/switch/[slug]` result pages, making the parts catalog a first-class editorial surface. The pending `/parts` browse landing [6.0] further elevates catalog discoverability. Both surfaces assume readers can find part detail pages — if /search can't surface them, the discovery triangle (quiz → result → /parts → /search → detail) has a broken spoke.
- rationale: The gap is concrete: `SearchDocument` type has no `kind`, no manufacturer, no entity spec data — all article-only fields. Extending the index to include entity records as a second document type (`PartSearchDocument: { id, slug, kind, name, manufacturer, type, tags }`) closes the gap with minimal architectural change. The `/search` results UI gains a `<PartResult>` card variant below article results.
- proposed scope (1 phase):
  1. Extend `generate-search-index.mts` to call `getAllSwitches()`, `getAllKeycapSets()`, `getAllBoards()` and add entity records as `PartSearchDocument`. Index fields: `name` (boost 4), `manufacturer` (boost 3), `type` (boost 2), `tags` (boost 2).
  2. Extend `runtime.ts`: add `PartSearchDocument` type and `PartSearchHit`; ship a `searchParts()` function (parallel to `searchArticles()`) or merge into a discriminated-union `search()` — implementer picks the least-disruptive shape.
  3. `/search` results UI: add a `<PartResult>` card below article hits when part results exist. Simple card: name, kind chip, manufacturer, link to `/part/[kind]/[slug]`.
  4. `apps/e2e/tests/search.spec.ts`: assert searching "Gateron" surfaces a part result linking to `/part/switch/gateron-oil-king`.
  5. `pnpm verify` green gate.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — extends Phase 6 search; no URL contract change; no schema change; `SearchDocument` type is additive only.

### [ ] [score 5.5] Vitest coverage CI gate — add per-workspace thresholds to lock in the post-test-drive completeness
- proposed: 2026-05-19, expand pass 17
- source signals:
  - **Commit-pattern signal (G — 22+ consecutive test commits)**: The systematic test-coverage drive spans passes 14–17. 22+ paired audit+test commits addressed every previously untested foundational module across all 6 workspaces — `@thock/data`/`@thock/content` loaders and caching contracts, validation infra (`walkAll`, `validateAll`, `paths.ts`), MDX components (Callout, Caption, PullQuote, PartReference, ArticleBody, Source.tsx), quiz orchestrator, search runtime (SearchPanel), Trends Tracker helpers. This is the longest single-category iterate drain in the project history. No vitest config has a `coverage` section — new code can ship without tests and the iterate loop catches it reactively (audit notice → file row → drain = 2–3 ticks per gap).
  - **Post-drive completion signal (this pass)**: The current iterate audit found no F-category (test) findings ≥ 3.0. This is the first tick since pass 14 where coverage is genuinely current across all workspaces. The natural engineering response to "we just filled all coverage gaps" is a gate that prevents them reopening.
- rationale: Without a threshold, every new phase that ships code without unit tests goes undetected until the next iterate audit. With per-workspace thresholds, CI fails immediately when a new commit introduces uncovered code — catching it in the same tick instead of 2–3 ticks later. The 22+ drain commits demonstrate the value: proactive enforcement would have prevented most of that drain. Proposed starting thresholds (statements 60%, functions 70%, lines 65%) are conservative enough to not block any current phase's shipping pattern while still catching "zero tests for new feature" cases. Per-workspace (not global rollup) so thin packages like `tokens` aren't held to the same bar as `packages/data`.
- proposed scope (1 phase):
  1. Add `coverage: { provider: 'v8', reporter: ['text', 'html'], thresholds: { statements: 60, functions: 70, lines: 65 } }` to all 6 vitest workspace configs. Thresholds calibrated per-workspace against current coverage snapshot at implementation time — the numbers above are starting estimates; the implementer adjusts to green before committing.
  2. Add `pnpm test:coverage` script at root workspace: `vitest run --coverage` across all workspaces. Additive alongside `pnpm test:run` — verify gate retains `test:run` (faster, no v8 overhead); CI calls `:coverage` separately.
  3. Add a `coverage` step to `.github/workflows/march.yml` (or new `coverage.yml`) that runs `pnpm test:coverage` on push to `main`. Runs in parallel with deploy-check; a threshold failure surfaces as a CI annotation without blocking the deploy.
  4. `plan/bearings.md` "Verify gate" section: one-liner noting the coverage thresholds so future phases know new code needs tests.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — additive only; verify gate (`pnpm verify`) is unchanged; no URL contract change; no schema change.

### [ ] [score 6.5] Critique gate diagnostic — `/critique` has not fired in 53 days / 1091 commits despite Step 2's dispatch condition being trivially satisfied on every cloud tick
- proposed: 2026-07-03, digest (first nightly pass)

  - **Pulse signal (dominant)**: `plan/CRITIQUE.md`'s header reads "Last pass: 2026-05-10T20:35:00Z at commit 931c8a7 / Pass count: 11" — unchanged as of this digest, 53 days and 1091 commits (`git rev-list --count 931c8a7..HEAD`) later. `skills/march.md` Step 2's dispatch condition is an OR of three sub-conditions ("current commit ≥12 commits after Last-pass commit, OR Last-pass >24h ago, OR Last-pass 'never' + phase 5+ shipped") — the ≥24h leg alone has been true on every cloud tick since roughly 2026-05-11T20:35, yet the header never advanced past pass 11.
  - **Ruled out (B — process of elimination against march's own logged conditions)**: (a) Step 1 triage preemption — `GH_TOKEN` is unavailable in cloud per essentially every expand-pass signal-audit note in this file ("triage unavailable (GH_TOKEN unavailable in cloud)"), so Step 1 always falls through to Step 2 on cloud ticks; (b) a blocked HIGH critique row — expand-pass signal audits have read "CRITIQUE.md 0 Pending rows" on nearly every pass across the window, so Step 2's condition 3 (don't preempt an in-flight HIGH drain) isn't the blocker; (c) a red deploy — `pnpm deploy:check` has read green at every digest/expand checkpoint spot-checked in the window.

The critique gate was already ~44 days / ~950 commits stale *before* march ever stopped ticking — this is a standing mistuning of the gate itself, not a symptom of the outage.
- rationale: With triage-preemption and the HIGH-row-block both ruled out and deploy green throughout, Step 2's OR-condition should have dispatched `/critique` on the very next eligible tick after 2026-05-11T20:35, and then repeatedly every ~12 commits or 24h thereafter — hundreds of eligible cloud ticks in the window. It never did. Two live hypotheses: (a) an implementation bug in how Step 2 is actually evaluated at runtime — possibly related to the same skill file describing the cadence as "≥12 commits + ≥24h spacing" (read as AND) in its own Purpose section while Step 2's body spells out an OR, an internal inconsistency that could be resolved either way depending on which was actually implemented; or (b) `/critique` is being dispatched but silently no-op'ing or erroring before it can update the `plan/CRITIQUE.md` header, with the failure swallowed non-fatally. A months-stale fresh-eyes queue is exactly the blind spot `/critique` exists to prevent — roughly 1091 commits of site surface area have shipped unreviewed by an external-observer pass.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — (1) resolve the Purpose-section-vs-Step-2-body ambiguity (AND vs. OR) to a single unambiguous condition, matching whichever cadence was actually intended; (2) add a one-line trace log inside Step 2 (e.g. an appended run-log line: "critique gate evaluated: <bool>, reason: <condition-that-fired-or-didn't>") so the next multi-week gap is diagnosable from run logs instead of inferred after the fact from a stale header; (3) manually trigger one `/critique` pass to break the freeze and re-baseline `plan/CRITIQUE.md`'s header; (4) if the freeze recurs after (1) and (2) ship, that isolates the fault to `/critique` itself rather than march's dispatch condition, and narrows the next investigation to `skills/critique.md`.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — skill-file + logging change only; no route/schema/URL contract change.

Demand is theoretical (no CRITIQUE or AUDIT finding has called this out) — the signal is spec-backed, not reader-surfaced. `/oversight` to weigh theoretical vs. concrete demand before promoting.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — (1) add `accessory` to `PackageSchema.kind` enum in `packages/data/src/schemas/`; regenerate JSON Schema; (2) `data/accessories/<slug>.json` for 5–8 seed records (stabilizer, lube, gasket foam, spring, cable — scout researches names + manufacturers + typical prices); (3) extend `/part/[kind]/[slug]` to accept `kind=accessory`; update `getAllParts()` / `getPartBySlug()` loaders to include accessories; (4) `/parts` browse landing gains "Accessories" section; (5) `apps/e2e/tests/parts.spec.ts` extended; sitemap + canonical-urls updated; `bearings.md` parts URL contract gains `/part/accessory/[slug]`.

- estimated phases: 1

Still iterate-shaped; four variants now documented.

### [score —] "Find your switch" interactive recommender — phase 33 (user-requested fun phase)

  - **Mechanic**: 4–5 single-select questions — sound profile (thock / clack / silent), actuation feel (linear / tactile / clicky), hand fatigue tolerance (light / medium / heavy spring), primary use (typing / gaming / mixed), budget tier (optional). Each answer applies weighted filters/scores over `getAllSwitches()`; results render the top 2–3 matches as cards linking to their existing `/part/switch/[slug]` pages (reuses phase 21 surfaces — no new detail pages).

Component split into small files (QuizStep, ResultCard, the page) per the build-plan style guardrails — no jam-packed single file.
  - **Discovery + SEO**: sitemap entry for `/quiz/switch`; canonical-urls + page-reads fixtures extended so the smoke walker covers it; `WebApplication` or `Quiz`-flavored JSON-LD (implementer picks the closest schema.org type at brief time). Add a small "Not sure where to start? Find your switch →" affordance somewhere honest (e.g. the future `/parts` index when it lands, or the switches-tag page) — keep it to one entry point, no nav-bar churn.
  - **e2e**: `apps/e2e/tests/quiz.spec.ts` — walk the quiz (answer each step, assert a result card with a `/part/switch/` href appears), assert no horizontal scroll at 375px, assert JSON-LD shape.
  - **No analytics special-casing**: page-level GTM already covers it; respects the existing `DISABLE_ANALYTICS=1` e2e gate.

### [score 7.0] Content-velocity queue auto-refill — make the Rule-1/2/3/4 content-gap queue self-replenishing
- promoted: 2026-05-14 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- assigned phase: **30**
- promotion decisions (locked at /oversight time):
  - **Helper location**: ship at `scripts/content-gap-survey.mjs` (not `@thock/content` export). Keeps the surface minimal — the helper is operational tooling for skills, not application API.
  - **Rule 4 (gap-fill) scope**: fires only as tie-breaker between Rule-1 candidates, never as a pillar-agnostic standalone row. Keeps the queue editorially coherent — gap-fill is a scheduling preference, not a shipping reason on its own.
  - **Rule 1 algorithm**: sliding 30d window per pillar; comfortable (≥2) → no row; hot pursuit (=1) → score 7.0; critical hot pursuit (=0) → score 9.5. Pillar selection on multi-cold: oldest most-recent publishedAt → lowest window count → prominence (Trends > News > Ideas > Deep Dives > Guides). Window cutoff, floor, and score values are bearings constants; helper reads from a single named-constants block (mirrored from bearings.md § Rule 1).
  - **Skill amendments**: `skills/ship-content.md` Step 8 invokes the helper post-drain and writes the next row into `plan/AUDIT.md` in the same `audit:` follow-up commit (one row per drain — no pre-fill). `skills/march.md` Step 3b.5 invokes the helper inline on empty queue before falling through to `/expand`.
  - **Verify gate**: two unit tests — (a) "1 article in 30d, deep-dives" → rule=1 pillar='deep-dives' score=7.0; (b) "0 articles in 30d, news" → score=9.5 with critical-hot-pursuit framing.
  - **Brief drafting**: drafted on-demand by `/ship-a-phase`.
- original signals + scope: see git history of this file at `ceefc38^` (pass-7 row); current bearings reframe makes Rule 1 algorithm sliding-window, fully captured in the promotion decisions above.

### [score 5.5] Streaming `<main>` landmark architectural call — Path (a) per-route `<main>` ownership
- promoted: 2026-05-10 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- assigned phase: **22**
- promotion decisions (locked at /oversight time):
  - **Path (a) locked**: move `<main>` from `apps/web/src/app/layout.tsx` to each route's `page.tsx`. Each `loading.tsx` also wraps its skeleton in `<main>`. Standard Next 15 + App Router pattern; preserves the per-route loading-skeleton UX while restoring SSR a11y-tree integrity.
  - **Why not Path (b)**: dropping `loading.tsx` files would lose the per-route perceived-speed win; restructuring per-route ownership has no downside trade-off in thock's footprint.
  - **Verify gate**: e2e adds `await expect(page.locator('main')).toHaveCount(1)` per canonical URL after the move. The smoke walker's existing `<h1>` assertion should be unaffected.
  - **Brief drafting**: drafted on-demand by `/ship-a-phase` (or pre-warmed by `/plan-a-phase phase 22`).
- original signals + scope: see `## Pending` row that was moved here on promotion. Closes the [needs-user-call] [HIGH] CRITIQUE row #22 from pass 7 (now reclassified `[x]` with promotion pointer).

### [score 7.0] Group-buy hero art — schema additive + retrofit + durable shipping rule
- promoted: 2026-05-10 via `/oversight` (this commit, in response to user observation)
- assigned phase: **23**
- promotion decisions (locked at /oversight time):
  - **Mirror the article hero-art directive**: every group buy (current and future) gets a hero SVG generated by `brander`, stored under `apps/web/public/group-buy-art/<vendor>-<slug>.svg`, with a sibling `<vendor>-<slug>.svg.json` provenance file. The `bearings.md` "Article hero art" section gets a sibling subsection "Group-buy hero art" that codifies this as a durable rule (this commit ships that section update).
  - **Schema additive**: `packages/data/src/schemas/group-buy.ts` gets a `heroImage: string?` field (Zod additive, optional). The existing `imageUrl` field stays — that's vendor-supplied product imagery, not the loop-generated hero. `heroImage` is the loop's editorial illustration.
  - **Render surfaces**: `/group-buys` cards, home `<GroupBuysWidget>` rows, and any `<TrackerRow>` that tags a group buy. All three render `heroImage` if present; fall back to a coral-tinted placeholder block if absent (so a partial backfill doesn't leave broken-image holes).
  - **Backfill scope**: 6 existing records in `data/group-buys/` need hero art (cannonkeys-nyawice, kbdfans-gmk-cyl-greg-2, kbdfans-gmk-cyl-ishtar-r2, kbdfans-gmk-cyl-king-of-the-seas, kbdfans-gsk-sweet-nightmare, wuque-studio-paper80-whatever-studio). `brander` renders 6 SVGs; subject mapping per kind (board → keyboard outline; keycap-set → keycap profile silhouette; switch → switch cross-section if a future GB targets one).
  - **Going-forward rule**: `skills/ship-data.md` gets a one-liner amendment so any new group-buy record committed via `/ship-data` bundles a `brander` invocation in the same commit, with `heroImage` set in the JSON. This mirrors the article-hero rule from phases 5+ (content-curator + brander as one bundle). Phase 23 ships the amendment as part of the brief execution.
  - **Brief drafting**: drafted on-demand by `/ship-a-phase` (or pre-warmed by `/plan-a-phase phase 23`).
- source signal: user-spotted via `/oversight` 2026-05-10T14:18Z — "all group bys on /group-buys need to show an image" + "generate hero art per group by when they are added ALWAYS just like we do for other content (make this a rule in your shipping)".
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none with `bearings.md` (extends the existing hero-art directive); none with the URL contract (no new routes); the schema additive is additive (nullable field, backwards-compatible).

## Rejected

### [score 4.5] Article series navigation — optional series frontmatter + prev/next reader affordance
- rejected: 2026-06-11 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- reason: sat below the promotion line since pass 94 (~8 days, ~30 expand passes) without score movement. The reader-path concern it targets is partially served today by the Related Articles rail and will be further served by phase 39 (prose cross-link auditor), which mechanically links companion articles — including the builder-anatomy sequence that motivated this candidate. A `series` frontmatter concept can be re-proposed if a genuinely ordered multi-part series is ever commissioned editorially; the current corpus pattern is thematic clustering, not sequenced parts.
- user answer at /oversight 2026-06-11: "Reject the two 4.5s".

### [score 4.5] Orphan parts editorial baseline — targeted articles for catalog parts with zero editorial cross-links
- rejected: 2026-06-11 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- reason: sat below the promotion line since pass 112. Commissioning articles to serve catalog records inverts the editorial direction — content should drive data, not backfill it. Rule-1 content velocity (~1 article per 3–4 days) plus the phase 38 mentionedParts gate will organically absorb orphan parts as future articles naturally mention them; parts that never earn a prose mention don't warrant commissioned coverage. Detail pages for orphan parts remain reachable via `/parts`, kind indexes, search, and the quiz.
- user answer at /oversight 2026-06-11: "Reject the two 4.5s".

### [score 6.5] React #418 hydration flake — dedicated investigation phase
- rejected: 2026-05-11 via `/oversight` (this commit) — **self-resolved**
- reason: pass-6 status update (commit `ec8d4c0`) recorded the flake had not been observed in 10+ consecutive parallel verify runs. Confirmed via /oversight: phase 16's PageStub-to-real-page replacement (`f3e5bac`) is the load-bearing fix — once every dynamic-data route had a real page (not the stub with its client/server-divergent state), the second hydration source the dfa5596 TZ patch couldn't reach went away. Serial-fallback mitigation is no longer the established per-tick pattern. The AUDIT.md row tracking this is cleared in the same commit.
- promotion path no longer needed: no investigation phase required.
